  > Key findings so far:
  > 
  > 1. The preserve endpoint in abnormal traces shows:
  >    - loadgenerator spans with status_code "Error" and NO HTTP response status code (null) - meaning the request timed out
  >    - avg_duration is ~20 seconds (20001327209 nanoseconds ≈ 20 seconds) - this is clearly a timeout
  >    - ts-ui-dashboard responds with 200 but also takes ~20 seconds
  > 
  > 2. The logs show:
  >    - ts-delivery-service has ERROR logs (48 ERRORs)
  >    - ts-food-service has ERROR logs (31 ERRORs)
  >    - ts-notification-service has ERROR logs (48 ERRORs)
  >    - ts-order-service has WARN logs (70 WARNs)
  >    - ts-order-other-service has WARN logs (132 WARNs)
  > 
  > The preserve endpoint calls ts-ui-dashboard which calls ts-preserve-service. The issue seems to be:
  > - loadgenerator gets Error (timeout) - 20 second requests
  > - ts-ui-dashboard also takes 20 seconds
  > 
  > But ts-ui-dashboard shows HTTP 200 responses... so it might be completing but very slowly.
  >

  > 1. Find what ts-ui-dashboard calls when serving /api/v1/preserveservice/preserve

  > 3. Check what's happening with ts-preserve-service specifically

  >    - ts-config-service: 48 drops
  >    - ts-payment-service: 42 drops
  >    - ts-food-service: 38 drops
  > 
  > These are network drops FROM these services. The destination is null which means these packets are being dropped by the network. `hubble_drop_total` records packets dropped by Cilium network policy or other network issues.
  > 
  > This is very significant! ts-security-service has 634 network drops, ts-basic-service has 263. These drops could explain why outgoing calls from these services are failing.
  > 
  > But wait - I need to compare this with the normal period to understand if these are abnormally high.
  > 
  > Also, I need to understand the direction: `attr_source` = the pod that's sourcing these packets that are being dropped. So packets FROM ts-security-service are being dropped at destination (null destination means the destination isn't visible/reachable).
  > 
  > Actually, the `attr_destination = null` and `attr_source = ts4/ts-security-service-...` suggests that the Hubble metric is tracking packets FROM ts-security-service going to null destinations (unreachable/dropped).

  > This could mean ts-security-service is trying to connect to services that are unreachable, causing connection timeouts.

  > 2. ts-preserve-service client span calling ts-seat-service (also 20 seconds)
  > 
  > would be expected to time out after 20 seconds, and NEITHER would be exported to the telemetry backend (they'd be dropped/abandoned spans).
  > 
  > This makes perfect sense! The trace data we see is ONLY what was successfully exported. If a span takes > 20 seconds (the timeout), it gets abandoned and never exported. So:
  > - ts-preserve-service's server span: abandoned (takes 20s)

#### Round 33  [stage=-]
- think_tool:
  > Very revealing comparison for ts-seat-service:
  > 
  > **Normal period** (ts-seat-service metrics):
  > - container.cpu.usage: avg 0.487 cores, max 1.4 cores
  > - jvm.system.cpu.load_1m: avg 11.8, max 23.3
  > - jvm.cpu.recent_utilization: avg 0.0036 (0.36%)
  > - container.memory.rss: 744MB avg, 750MB max
  > 
  > **Abnormal period** (ts-seat-service metrics):
  > - container.cpu.usage: avg 0.072 cores, max 0.516 cores (SIGNIFICANTLY LOWER!)
  > - jvm.system.cpu.load_1m: avg 5.35, max 8.9 (LOWER!)
  > - jvm.cpu.recent_utilization: avg 0.00066 (0.066%) (SIGNIFICANTLY LOWER!)
  > - container.memory.rss: 752MB avg, 755MB max (similar)
  > 
  > This is striking! In the abnormal period:
  > - ts-seat-service CPU usage is 7x LOWER than normal
  > - The system CPU load is much lower too (5.35 vs 11.8)
  > 
  > This means ts-seat-service is MUCH LESS BUSY in the abnormal period. It's not creating seats because it's receiving fewer requests (consistent with the trace evidence showing no create seat spans).
  > 
  > The service is running (processing left_tickets requests), but the create seat path is not being exercised. This strongly suggests that the issue is UPSTREAM of ts-seat-service - specifically ts-preserve-service is not even getting to the point of calling ts-seat-service.
  > 
  > Wait - but we established that ts-preserve-service's server span is missing (not exported due to 20s hang), and the early sub-calls complete quickly. So ts-preserve-service IS starting the preserve workflow but then either:
  > 1. It crashes/exits before reaching ts-seat-service
  > 2. It hangs somewhere before reaching ts-seat-service
  > 
  > But we see ts-preserve-service calling ts-travel-service (63ms) which is AFTER ts-security-service and ts-contacts-service in the flow. In normal flow, the order is:
  > 1. ts-security-service check
  > 2. ts-contacts-service get
  > 3. ts-travel-service trip_detail
  > 4. ts-seat-service create seat (POST /seats)
  > 5. ts-order-service create order
  > 
  > So ts-preserve-service gets to step 3 (ts-travel-service) but NOT step 4 (ts-seat-service). The call to ts-seat-service must be hanging.
  > 
  > But why is ts-seat-service's CPU so much lower? If ts-preserve-service is hanging calling ts-seat-service, there should be some goroutines/threads in ts-seat-service processing...
  > 
  > Unless the request to ts-seat-service never arrives! Maybe the connection from ts-preserve-service to ts-seat-service is being dropped at the network level (Cilium policy or network issue), so ts-seat-service never sees the request.
  > 
  > Evidence:
  > 1. ts-preserve-service has 62 hubble_drop_total (vs 43 in normal, +44%)
  > 2. The specific call to ts-seat-service for create is missing from both ts-preserve-service spans AND ts-seat-service spans
  > 3. ts-seat-service CPU is very low (not processing create requests)
  > 
  > This points to a NETWORK issue between ts-preserve-service and ts-seat-service. The SYN packet or HTTP request from ts-preserve-service to ts-seat-service is being dropped/delayed.
  > 
  > But wait - ts-travel-service's internal sub-calls to ts-seat-service (for left_tickets) ARE working (12ms). So ts-seat-service IS reachable... but from ts-travel-service, not necessarily from ts-preserve-service.
  > 
  > Actually, I need to think about Cilium network policies. Could there be a network policy that allows ts-travel-service → ts-seat-service but NOT ts-preserve-service → ts-seat-service?
  > 
  > OR - could ts-seat-service's port for the create endpoint be different from the left_tickets endpoint? No, they'd use the same service port.
  > 
  > Wait - let me reconsider. Maybe ts-preserve-service hangs for a different reason. What if the ts-preserve-service is waiting for something BEFORE it calls ts-seat-service? 
  > 
  > Actually... let me look at this differently. ts-seat-service's low CPU in abnormal period means fewer requests in total. But ts-seat-service still handles 422 left_tickets requests. Those come from ts-travel-service calls. And the ts-travel-service calls are working (they respond in 63ms in the abnormal trace).
  > 
  > But wait - there's a discrepancy. In the normal traces, ts-seat-service has 3172 left_tickets + 156 create = 3328 POST spans. In abnormal: 422 left_tickets + 0 create = 422 POST spans. That's roughly 1/8th of the normal volume!
  > 
  > This huge reduction in volume (3328 → 422 spans) is consistent with the shorter abnormal period (which has 23,018 total spans vs normal's 189,718 spans = ~1/8 ratio). So the ratio is actually proportional!
  > 
  > So the absolute number of left_tickets calls is proportional to normal. What's abnormal is that create seat calls = 0 in the abnormal period.

#### Round 49  [stage=-]
- **hypothesis_at_round**: `ts-seat-service`
- think_tool:
  > Key findings:
  > 1. **MySQL** is on **worker5**, NOT worker3! And MySQL metrics look completely normal (low CPU, low memory use, no errors).
  > 
  > 2. Worker3 hosts **ts-seat-service** AND **ts-notification-service**. The worker3 node has a system CPU load of 5.35 average (very low!) in the abnormal period.
  > 
  > 3. ts-notification-service is also on worker3. It has ERROR logs: "Failed to check/redeclare auto-delete queue(s)" - AMQP connection issues.
  > 
  > Now let me think about this differently. ts-notification-service and ts-delivery-service both have AMQP errors. These services typically receive order notifications via message queue (RabbitMQ/AMQP) when an order is created. 
  > 
  > But WAIT - these AMQP errors are in ts-delivery-service and ts-notification-service. How does this relate to the preserve flow?
  > 
  > Actually, I wonder - does ts-preserve-service or ts-seat-service make an AMQP call during the booking process? Some microservice booking flows use:
  > 1. HTTP calls for synchronous parts
  > 2. AMQP for async notifications
  > 
  > But the hanging is happening SYNCHRONOUSLY (the whole request hangs for 20 seconds). 
  > 
  > Wait - actually, some services call RabbitMQ (AMQP) SYNCHRONOUSLY as part of order creation. If ts-seat-service or ts-order-service tries to send a message to RabbitMQ after creating a seat, and RabbitMQ is unavailable, the call would hang.
  > 
  > BUT - looking at the logs, both ts-delivery-service and ts-notification-service have "Failed to check/redeclare auto-delete queue(s)" errors. This is a RabbitMQ/AMQP connectivity error. These services are CONSUMERS of messages. If they can't connect to RabbitMQ, they can't receive messages.
  > 
  > If the producer (ts-order-service or ts-preserve-service) also tries to connect to RabbitMQ and fails... that could cause the 20-second hang!
  > 
  > But wait, the ts-preserve-service and ts-order-service don't appear to make AMQP calls in the normal traces (only HTTP calls are visible).
  > 
  > Actually, let me step back. What if the core issue is SIMPLER than I think?
  > 
  > Looking at the evidence:
  > 1. ts-seat-service is working for left_tickets
  > 2. ts-preserve-service → ts-seat-service TCP traffic is 10x higher per unit time in abnormal
  > 3. ts-seat-service has NO create seat spans in abnormal
  > 4. The whole preserve request hangs for exactly 20 seconds
  > 
  > The 20-second hang is VERY PRECISE. This looks like an HTTP client timeout. The default Spring Boot RestTemplate or WebClient timeout is often 20 seconds or similar.
  > 
  > What if:
  > - ts-preserve-service calls ts-seat-service POST /seats
  > - ts-seat-service accepts the TCP connection (SYN-ACK)
  > - ts-seat-service queues the request but can't process it (thread pool exhausted?)
  > - After 20 seconds, the connection times out
  > 
  > If ts-seat-service's thread pool is exhausted for the create endpoint, it would accept the TCP connection but not process it. This would explain:
  > - TCP traffic exists between preserve and seat (connection accepted)
  > - No processing span in ts-seat-service
  > - 20-second wait
  > 
  > But ts-seat-service has LOW CPU and few threads (avg 5.875, max 13). That doesn't suggest thread exhaustion.
  > 
  > Actually wait - max 13 threads and avg 5.875... but in NORMAL the max was 13 too. So thread count is similar.
  > 
  > OK let me try a completely different approach. Let me look at the PROCESS_PAUSED or network delay scenario. What if ts-seat-service's pod was paused (SIGSTOP/SIGCONT)?
  > 
  > Actually, I think the key clue I'm missing is about the SEQUENCE of calls in ts-preserve-service. Let me look at this from the normal trace again.
  > 
  > In the normal trace (ordered by time), looking at the spans AFTER the ts-travel-service call:
  > - OFFSET 30: ts-contacts-service spans, ts-travel-service spans
  > - OFFSET 50: ts-station-service, ts-train-service, ts-route-service (sub-calls from ts-basic-service inside ts-travel-service)
  > 
  > But these offsets are by ORDER BY time. The spans I see at offset 50 have VERY SHORT durations (1-6ms), suggesting they're completing BEFORE the 63ms travel call is even done (they're sub-spans within it).
  >

  >

  > - ts-preserve-service has 3 OUTGOING calls in the abnormal trace (security, contacts, travel)
  > - In normal, it would have 5+ outgoing calls (security, contacts, travel, seat_create, order_create)
  > - The missing calls are: seat_create, order_create (and maybe price?)
  > 
  > The FIRST missing call after travel is the seat create. If the seat create hangs, all subsequent calls also don't happen.

  >

  >

  > 
  > But the ts-seat-service CREATE is not in the abnormal trace. So after ts-price-service, ts-preserve-service calls ts-seat-service, and THAT hangs.

  > 
  > Actually, looking at it differently: ALL the services that are in the abnormal trace are probably there because they were called from ts-travel-service's internal flow (which completes in 63ms). ts-price-service might be called by ts-travel-service, not directly by ts-preserve-service.
  > 
  > So the full picture might be:
  > - ts-preserve-service calls: security → contacts → travel (which internally calls basic → seat_left_tickets → price → route → station → train → etc.)
  > - After travel returns (63ms), ts-preserve-service tries to call seat_create → HANGS for 20s
  > 
  > This is my best hypothesis. The root cause is something that causes ts-seat-service's create endpoint to be inaccessible/unresponsive specifically from ts-preserve-service.
  >

  >

  > 1. ts-seat-service create (126ms)
  > 2. ts-order-service create order (?)
  > 
  > If ts-order-service hangs for 20 seconds...
  > 
  > But then why are there no ts-seat-service create spans? If ts-seat-service COMPLETED, we'd see its span exported. But there's NO ts-seat-service create span in abnormal.
  > 
  > So the FIRST hung call is definitely the seat create. ts-order-service comes AFTER.
  > 
  > OK so my conclusion stands:
  > - ts-preserve-service calls ts-seat-service (POST /seats) and hangs
  > - This causes the entire preserve request to timeout
  > 
  > The root cause is the unavailability/slowness of ts-seat-service's create endpoint, which propagates to ts-preserve-service, ts-ui-dashboard, and the loadgenerator.
  > 
  > But the UNDERLYING cause of ts-seat-service's create endpoint hanging... the evidence points to:
  > 1. TCP connections ARE being established (bi-directional traffic exists)
  > 2. ts-seat-service has low load (not overloaded)
  > 3. ts-seat-service logs only show left_tickets activity
  > 4. The node (worker3) has low CPU load (5.35 avg)
  > 
  > This pattern is consistent with a PROCESS PAUSE scenario: ts-seat-service's JVM was briefly paused (e.g., due to SIGSTOP or a very long GC pause that isn't captured), causing incoming HTTP requests to queue up and eventually timeout.
  > 
  > OR - it could be a network issue on worker3 specifically for the path ts-preserve-service → ts-seat-service.
  > 
  > Actually wait - I just realized something. The hubble metrics show TCP traffic but NOT whether those connections succeed. The fact that ts-preserve-service → ts-seat-service has MUCH MORE TCP traffic in abnormal could mean:
  > - Each individual preserve request tries the seat create connection
  > - The connection attempt hangs for ~20 seconds
  > - During this 20 seconds, TCP keepalives or retransmissions generate more TCP flag events
  > 
  > This is actually consistent with NETWORK_DELAY! If there's a network delay (packet loss or delay) on the path from ts-preserve-service (worker6) to ts-seat-service (worker3), TCP retransmissions would occur, inflating the TCP flag count.
  > 
  > Let me check if there's any network latency metric between worker6 and worker3 in the abnormal period.
  > 
  > Actually, I should just look at whether there are NETWORK_DELAY or NETWORK_LOSS metrics in the abnormal period for worker3 or for ts-seat-service.
  > 
  > But before spending another tool call, let me look at what I know:
  > 1. ts-seat-service pod has 0 network errors
  > 2. worker3 has low CPU load (5.35)
  > 3. TCP traffic between ts-preserve-service and ts-seat-service is 10x higher per unit time
  > 
  > The 10x higher TCP traffic suggests retransmissions (network delay/loss). This is the strongest evidence of NETWORK_DELAY.
  > 
  > Given all the evidence, the most likely root cause is:
  > - **ts-seat-service** experiencing HIGH_LATENCY or NETWORK_DELAY
  > - The network path from ts-preserve-service (worker6) to ts-seat-service (worker3) has delays/issues
  > - This causes ts-preserve-service to hang when calling seat create
  > - Which causes ts-ui-dashboard and loadgenerator to experience HIGH_LATENCY/TIMEOUT
  > 
  > Actually, wait. Let me reconsider whether the root cause is ts-seat-service itself or the NETWORK between the two services.

  > Converting 2025-07-25T05:06:33 to unix timestamp:
  > 2025-07-25 = year 2025, month 7, day 25

  > 
  > Let me verify: 2025-07-25 05:06:33 UTC
  > - 2025-01-01 00:00:00 UTC = 1735689600
  > - Days from Jan 1 to Jul 25: 31 (Jan) + 28 (Feb) + 31 (Mar) + 30 (Apr) + 31 (May) + 30 (Jun) + 24 (Jul) = 205 days
  > - 205 × 86400 = 17,712,000
  > - 1735689600 + 17,712,000 = 1,753,401,600
  > - Add 5:06:33 = 5×3600 + 6×60 + 33 = 18000 + 360 + 33 = 18393
  > - 1,753,401,600 + 18393 = 1,753,419,993
  >

  **Root Cause**: ts-seat-service (specifically its seat creation endpoint `POST /api/v1/seatservice/seats`)
  
  **Evidence**:
  1. In normal traces: ts-seat-service has 156 successful seat creation spans (POST /seats)
  2. In abnormal traces: ts-seat-service has ZERO seat creation spans
  3. ALL TCP traffic to/from ts-seat-service is 11-15x higher per unit time in abnormal vs normal (indicating retransmissions/hung connections)
  4. The preserve request hangs for exactly ~20 seconds (HTTP timeout threshold)
  5. ts-preserve-service's sub-calls to security, contacts, and travel all complete quickly
  6. The NEXT call in the preserve flow after travel-service is seat-create - this is where it hangs
  
  **State Classification**:
  - ts-seat-service: HIGH_LATENCY (seat create endpoint unresponsive, causing timeouts)
  - ts-preserve-service: HIGH_LATENCY (waiting for ts-seat-service to respond)
  - ts-ui-dashboard: HIGH_LATENCY (waiting for ts-preserve-service)
  - loadgenerator: TIMEOUT (Error status after 20s wait)
  
  **Fault Propagation Path**:
  ts-seat-service (HIGH_LATENCY) → ts-preserve-service (HIGH_LATENCY) → ts-ui-dashboard (HIGH_LATENCY) → loadgenerator (TIMEOUT/Error)
  
  The root cause service is **ts-seat-service** - it originated the failure by being unresponsive for seat creation requests.
  
  **Timestamps**: The earliest anomalies start at 2025-07-25T05:06:33 UTC (from the logs).
  
  For the causal graph:
  - Nodes: ts-seat-service (HIGH_LATENCY), ts-preserve-service (HIGH_LATENCY), ts-ui-dashboard (HIGH_LATENCY)
  - Edges: ts-seat-service → ts-preserve-service → ts-ui-dashboard
  - Root cause: ts-seat-service
